Argument from Opposing Natures
First argument: from composition of opposing natures.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand why an entity composed of opposing natures requires an external conjoiner.

Core Idea
Opposing natures cannot unite by themselves.

Maturidi begins with a powerful observation: things with naturally repulsive qualities cannot assemble on their own. This leads to the necessity of a conjoiner. Let's examine the first proof.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage carefully
Read the Arabic for the first argument, then the translation. Notice the logical structure: premise, conclusion, and the invocation of divine success.
The phrase 'والله الموفق' is a common seal.
2
Identify the key terms
Focus on 'عين' (entity), 'طبائع متضادة' (opposing natures), and 'جامع' (conjoiner). Understand how they relate.
3
Reflect on the implication
Consider: if even a simple entity with opposing natures needs a conjoiner, how much more so the entire universe?

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وأيضا أن كل عين مما اجتمع فيه الطبائع المتضادة التي من طبعها التنافر لم يجز أن يكون بنفسه يجتمع ، ثبت أن له جامعا ، والله الموفق . وأيضا أن كل عين محتاج إلى آخر به يقوم ويبقى من الأغذية وغيرها مما لا يحتمل أن يبلغ علمه ما به بقاؤه ، أو كيف يستخرج ذلك ويكتسب ، فثبت أنه بعليم حكيم لا بنفسه ، وبالله النجاة والعصمة وأيضا أنه لو كان بنفسه لكان يبقى به ويكون على حد واحد يملك دل على أنه كان بغيره مع ، فلما تم ما لو كان وأيضا لا يخلو كونه بنفسه من أن كان بعد الوجود ، فيبطل كونه به ؛ لما كان موجودا بغيره ، أو قبله ، وما هو قبله كيف يوجد نفسه ، به قبل الوجود لتوهم أن لا يوجد فيكون عديما فاعلا وذلك محال . ويشهد لما ذكرنا أمر البناء والكتابة والسفن أنه لا يجوز كونها إلا بفاعل موجود ، فمثله ما نحن فيه . وبالله التوفيق.
Also, every individual entity in which opposing natures of innate repulsion are gathered cannot be self-assembling; so it is established that it has a conjoiner, and Allah is the grantor of success. Also, every individual entity is in need of another by which it stands and remains, from nourishments and other things whose knowledge of what sustains it cannot be attained, nor how to extract and acquire it; so it is established that it is through a Knowing, Wise [being], not by itself, and with Allah is deliverance and protection. Also, if it were by itself, it would persist by itself and be upon a single state [...]; this indicates that it was with another. Also, its being by itself cannot be free from being after existence, then its being by it would be invalid because it existed by another; or before it, and what is before it, how can it bring itself into existence before existence, leading to the assumption that it does not exist, thus it would be a non-existent agent, and that is impossible. And what supports what we have mentioned is the matter of buildings, writing, and ships: they cannot exist except through an existing agent; similarly is what we are discussing. And with Allah is success.
Source pages p. 617

Commentary
This passage presents a series of four interconnected arguments demonstrating that the world cannot be self-originating. The first argument is from composition: any entity composed of opposing natures cannot assemble itself; it requires a conjoiner. The second argument is from dependence: every entity relies on external sustenance and means for its survival, which it cannot know or acquire on its own, proving it depends on a Knowing, Wise being. The third argument, though partly garbled, posits that if something were self-subsistent, it would remain in one state, but observable change shows it is with another. The fourth argument eliminates temporal paradox: if something were self-originating, it would have to exist before itself to bring itself into existence, which is absurd. The passage concludes with an analogy: human artifacts like buildings, writing, and ships visibly require an agent; by analogy, the world must also have an agent. Each argument independently refutes the notion of self-origination, culminating in the affirmation that the world has a creator.

Key Terms
عين
طبائع متضادة
جامع

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some think order can emerge spontaneously from chaos without external cause.
Correction: The argument shows that opposing natures repulse each other, so a unifier is necessary.

Checkpoint
According to the first argument, why cannot an entity composed of opposing natures be self-assembling?
A) Because it would need a conjoiner due to natural repulsion.
B) Because it would need food to survive.
C) Because it would have to exist before itself.
D) Because it would remain in a single state.

Key Takeaway
Entities with opposing natures cannot self-assemble; they require an external conjoiner.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you feel torn between conflicting desires in your life, do you seek a unifying purpose from Allah, or do you assume you can reconcile them by yourself? This lesson shows that even in nature, opposing forces need an external conjoiner. Where is your conjoiner?
?
The universe's order proves it has a Conjoiner. Does your personal life bear witness to a single organizing principle rooted in your submission to Allah, or is it fragmented by competing loyalties? What would it mean for you to let Allah be the Jāmi‘ of your heart?
?
If you truly believe that nothing with opposing natures can come together without a Creator, then how do you explain the disorder in your own soul when you ignore Him? Are there areas where you have tried to force harmony through your own effort rather than turning to the One who holds all things together?

Argument from Dependence on Sustenance
Second argument: from need for external sustenance.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how every entity's need for external sustenance proves it depends on a Knowing, Wise being.

Core Idea
Everything relies on something else for survival.

The second argument shifts focus: every entity requires external things like food to survive, and it cannot know how to acquire them on its own. This points to a Wise Provider.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage

2
Analyze the dependency

3
Connect to the conclusion
The argument concludes that such dependence proves a Knowing, Wise being (عليم حكيم) is the source, not the entity itself.
The phrase 'وبالله النجاة والعصمة' is a prayer.

Arguments from Temporal Paradox and State Change
Third and fourth arguments: from state change and temporal paradox.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand why self-origination leads to absurdities like an entity causing itself before existing.

Core Idea
Self-origination implies logical contradictions.

The third and fourth arguments tackle the very idea of something bringing itself into existence. Maturidi shows that self-origination either requires an impossible temporal order or contradicts observable change.

Guided Path
1
Read the combined passage
This lesson covers two arguments. Read the Arabic and translation carefully, noting the conditional and paradoxical structure.
The third argument is partially garbled, but the core meaning is reconstructed.
2
Understand the temporal paradox
The fourth argument: if something were self-originating, it would have to exist before itself to act, which is impossible. Identify the reductio ad absurdum.
3
Reflect on the implications
Consider why this argument is powerful: it eliminates the idea of self-causation completely.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وأيضا أن كل عين مما اجتمع فيه الطبائع المتضادة التي من طبعها التنافر لم يجز أن يكون بنفسه يجتمع ، ثبت أن له جامعا ، والله الموفق . وأيضا أن كل عين محتاج إلى آخر به يقوم ويبقى من الأغذية وغيرها مما لا يحتمل أن يبلغ علمه ما به بقاؤه ، أو كيف يستخرج ذلك ويكتسب ، فثبت أنه بعليم حكيم لا بنفسه ، وبالله النجاة والعصمة وأيضا أنه لو كان بنفسه لكان يبقى به ويكون على حد واحد يملك دل على أنه كان بغيره مع ، فلما تم ما لو كان وأيضا لا يخلو كونه بنفسه من أن كان بعد الوجود ، فيبطل كونه به ؛ لما كان موجودا بغيره ، أو قبله ، وما هو قبله كيف يوجد نفسه ، به قبل الوجود لتوهم أن لا يوجد فيكون عديما فاعلا وذلك محال . ويشهد لما ذكرنا أمر البناء والكتابة والسفن أنه لا يجوز كونها إلا بفاعل موجود ، فمثله ما نحن فيه . وبالله التوفيق.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?

?
The passage argues that if something were self-subsisting, it would be 'upon a single state.' Think of a recent change in your own character or circumstances. Does that change not point to your own dependence? How does this humble you before the Unchanging Creator?
?
The fourth argument shows that bringing oneself into existence is absurd. Yet how often do you try to 'create' your own identity or worth apart from your Creator? What specific belief or habit must you abandon to acknowledge that your very existence is a gift from another?

Like artifacts, the world requires a maker.

The Wisdom in Creation Points to an Originator
Maturidi presents the argument from wisdom against self-origination.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how the intricate wisdom in every aspect of creation demonstrates that the world cannot be self-originating.

Core Idea
Every detail of creation contains wisdom beyond human grasp, proving a wise Originator.

Imam Maturidi begins by establishing that nothing in the world is devoid of profound wisdom. Even the most learned philosophers cannot fully comprehend the essence and manner of things. This universal wisdom is a clear sign that the world has a wise Originator. In this lesson, we explore the first argument: the argument from design.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage and translation
Read the Arabic passage once without analyzing. Then read the literal translation to grasp the meaning.
Notice that Maturidi emphasizes the inability of wise people to fully comprehend.
2
Identify Maturidi's claim about wisdom
Find the sentence that states that nothing in creation is free from wisdom. Reflect on what this implies about the cause of the world.
3
Reflect on human limitation
Consider why the fact that even the wisest cannot fully grasp the nature of things strengthens the argument for a creator.
This connects to the core idea that the originator must be all-wise.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قال أبو منصور رحمه الله : وأصل ذلك أنه لا يعانى منه شيء إلا فيه حكمة عجيبة ودلالة بديعة مما يعجز الحكماء عن إدراك / مائيته وكيفية خروجه على ما خرج، وعلم كل أحد منهم بقصور على ما عنده من الحكمة والعلم عن إدراك كنه ذلك ، فهذه الضرورة وغيرها دلالة حكمة مبدعها وخالقها ، ولا قوة إلا بالله وأيضا أنه لو جاز أن يكون العالم يبدأ من قبل نفسه بمرة لجائز أن يذهب كله بمرة ، فإذا لم يكن ، بل كان على الاختلاف حتى لم يكن تختلف عليه الأحوال إلا بالأغيار نحو حي يموت ، ومتفرق يجتمع ، وصغير يكبر ، وخبيث يطيب ، أبدا يتغير بأغيار تحدث ، فعلى ذلك جملته ، لا يحتمل أن يكون لا بغيره . ولو جاز ذا الجاز أن تتغير ألوان الثوب بنفسه لا بأصباغ ، أو السفينه تصير على ما هي عليها بذاتها ، فإذا لم تكن - ولا بد من عليم بنشئها ، قدير به يكون – فكذلك ما نحن فيه ، وبالله التوفيق
Abu Mansur – may Allah have mercy on him – said: The foundation of this is that nothing in it is free from a wondrous wisdom and an excellent indication, such that the wise are incapable of grasping its quiddity and how it emerges as it does, and every one of them knows his limitation relative to his wisdom and knowledge in perceiving the reality of that. So this necessity and other things are an indication of the wisdom of its Originator and Creator, and there is no power except with Allah. Also, if it were permissible for the world to begin by itself at once, then it would be permissible for it to perish entirely at once. But since it does not, rather it is in a state of change such that its states only change through external factors – like a living thing that dies, a scattered thing that gathers, a small thing that grows, a foul thing that becomes good – perpetually changing through new accidents, so in its entirety it cannot be without another. And if that were permissible, it would be permissible for the colors of a garment to change by themselves without dyes, or for a ship to become what it is by itself; but since that is not the case – and there must be a Knower of its origin, a Powerful by whom it is – so similarly is what we are discussing. And with Allah is success.
Source pages p. 617

Commentary
This passage advances two interconnected arguments. First, the argument from wisdom: every detail of creation contains an indescribable wisdom that even the wisest humans cannot fully grasp. This demonstrates that the world cannot be self-originating, because a self-originating entity would not produce such purposeful design. Second, the argument from persistence and change: if the world could begin by itself, it could also end by itself instantly. But we observe that the world persists through gradual changes, each change caused by external factors (e.g., birth, death, growth, decay). This continuous reliance on external causes proves the world cannot exist independently. The passage employs an analogy: just as the colors of a garment change only through dyes, and a ship requires a maker, so the world requires a creator. The conclusion is that the world is in constant need of an external agent, namely a wise and powerful creator.

Key Terms
حكمة
مبدع
خالق

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: One might think that complexity can arise from random chance without a designer.
Correction: Maturidi argues that the specific, ordered wisdom in every detail precludes self-origination, as self-origination would lack purpose.

Checkpoint
What does Maturidi claim about every aspect of creation?
A) It contains hidden wisdom.
B) It is random.
C) It is self-explanatory.
D) It changes continuously.

Key Takeaway
The pervasiveness of wisdom in creation is a direct proof that the world has a wise Originator and cannot be self-originating.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you observe the intricate details of your own body or the world around you, have you truly acknowledged the wisdom of the One who designed it? Or have you taken it for granted as a mere product of nature? This week, take one specific example (e.g., your heartbeat or the structure of a leaf) and consciously attribute it to Allah's wisdom in your heart.
?
The passage says even the wisest are incapable of grasping the true nature of things. How does this humble your own intellectual pride? In what area of your life do you need to admit your limitation before Allah and rely on His wisdom instead of your own understanding? Make a concrete plan to act on this this week.
?
If every detail in creation is filled with wisdom, then even the trials you face are not random. How does this truth change the way you will respond to a difficulty you are currently facing? Write down one trial and then ask Allah to help you see the wisdom in it.

Change and the Necessity of a Creator
Maturidi uses change and external causality to refute self-origination.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand why the world's constant change through external factors proves it requires a creator.

Core Idea
If the world could begin by itself, it could end by itself; but its gradual change shows dependence on external causes.

After establishing the argument from wisdom, Imam Maturidi presents a second proof: the argument from change and persistence. He argues that if the world were self-originating, it could vanish instantly. Instead, we observe gradual changes that require external factors. This section also includes a powerful analogy to clarify the point.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage and translation
Read the Arabic passage and translation together. Pay attention to the conditional statement and the examples.
2
Understand the conditional argument
Maturidi says if the world began by itself, it could also perish by itself instantly. This sets up a logical contrast with observation.
The argument is a reductio ad absurdum.
3
Observe the examples of change
List the changes mentioned: living→dead, scattered→gathered, small→growing, foul→good. Notice they all involve external factors (agyar).
4
Analyze the analogy
Compare the world to a garment's colors needing dyes and a ship needing a maker. This clarifies that the world cannot exist without a creator.
The analogy is a common method in kalam.

The World's Order Demands a Knowing and Powerful Creator
Maturidi argues from design against self-creation.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand why the order and design in the world cannot originate from an ignorant or incapable cause.

Core Idea
Evidence of knowledge in creation rules out self-causation.

Imam Maturidi presents a concise argument from design: the world's intricate order shows knowledge and power. Such a system cannot arise from an incapable or ignorant source. This lesson explores that logical inference.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage carefully
Read the Arabic passage once without trying to analyse it. Then read the translation. Notice how Maturidi uses the term 'far-fetched' (يُبْعَد) to initially distance the idea of self-creation.
2
Identify the evidence
Identify what Maturidi says is in the world that precludes self-creation: 'evidence of knowledge of what it is upon and power over it' (دلالة العلم بما هو عليه والقدرة عليه).
The world points to a knowing and powerful cause.
3
Reflect on the impossibility
Consider why an incapable or ignorant being cannot produce such order. Then reflect on the rhetorical escalation to a non-existent, perishing being.
The argument moves from impossibility to absurdity.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ويبعد أيضاً كون العالم بنفسه بما فيه من دلالة العلم بما هو عليه والقدرة عليه ، ومحال وجود مثله بعاجز جاهل ، فكيف بالمعدوم الفانى، وبالله التوفيق . ودلالة كون العالم لا من شيء هى حدوثها ، وقد بينا ذلك .
It is also far-fetched that the world is by itself, given what it contains of evidence of knowledge of what it is upon and power over it, and it is impossible for the like of it to exist from an incapable, ignorant being, so how about from a non-existent, perishing one? And with Allah is success. And the evidence that the world came from nothing is its origination (ḥudūth), and we have already explained that.
Source pages p. 618

Commentary
This brief passage presents a concise argument: the world exhibits clear signs of knowledge and power in its order and design. Such an organized system cannot proceed from an incapable or ignorant source, let alone from something that is non-existent or perishable. Therefore, the world cannot be self-caused or the product of chance. The passage then reiterates that the very fact that the world is originated (ḥudūth) – that it came into existence after not existing – is itself the evidence that it was created from nothing. This argument reinforces the previous ones by focusing on the attributes of knowledge and power manifest in creation, which demand a knowing and powerful creator.

Key Terms
علم (knowledge)
قدرة (power)
عاجز (incapable)
جاهل (ignorant)
معدوم (non-existent)

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some think that random processes or natural laws can produce the intricate order of the world without intelligence.
Correction: The passage argues that the evident knowledge and power in the world preclude a random, ignorant, or incapable cause. The order itself is proof of design.

Checkpoint
Why does the passage say the world cannot be by itself?
A) Because it contains evidence of knowledge and power.
B) Because it is permanent.
C) Because it changes gradually.
D) Because it is composed of opposing natures.

Key Takeaway
The world's evident knowledge and power prove it cannot be self-caused or from an ignorant source.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
If the order in your own body—your heartbeat, your thoughts, your very existence—is evidence of knowledge and power, how can you continue to live as if your life is accidental? What will you commit to acknowledging today about the One who designed you?
?
The text says it is impossible for an incapable or ignorant being to create such order. Do you ever attribute your successes or the blessings in your life to your own ability, luck, or natural processes? How does this passage expose that as a form of shirk? What one action can you take today to redirect all praise to the true Creator?
?
Consider the stark contrast: you were once non-existent and will one day perish. Yet you often live as if you are self-sufficient. How does the phrase 'فكيف بالمعدوم الفانى' strike your heart? What change in your daily routine can you make to remember that your existence is a gift from the Knowing, Powerful One?

Origination (Ḥudūth) as Evidence of Creation from Nothing
Maturidi states ḥudūth as the evidence for creation from nothing.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand that the world's origination (ḥudūth) is itself the evidence that it came into existence from nothing.

Core Idea
The world's beginning proves it was created from nothing.

Imam Maturidi reminds us that the very fact that the world originated—that it came to be after not existing—is the key evidence for creation ex nihilo. This lesson examines that concise statement.

Guided Path
1
Read the short passage
Read the Arabic sentence and its translation. Note the term 'dalāla' (evidence) and 'ḥudūth' (origination).
This is a very condensed statement.
2
Understand ḥudūth
Understand that ḥudūth means the world had a beginning in time. It came into existence after not existing.
3
Connect to the argument
Ask yourself: How does the fact that the world originated serve as evidence that it came from nothing? Reflect on the alternatives.
If the world had always existed, it would not need a cause; but since it began, it must have been brought into existence.

Source Text

The passage then reiterates that the very fact that the world is originated (ḥudūth) – that it came into existence after not existing – is itself the evidence that it was created from nothing. How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?

?

?
Māturīdī says the proof is ḥudūth. If someone asked you today, 'Why is there something rather than nothing?' would you answer with the logic of this passage, or do you still have doubts? What will you do to root those doubts out?

Shaytan's Deception and the Inconsistency of Denying Perception
Maturidi introduces shaytan's deception and argues that deniers of perception are inconsistent.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand Maturidi's argument that deniers of perception are inconsistent because they rely on perception in their daily lives, revealing that their denial stems from desire for pleasure rather than genuine ignorance.

Core Idea
Deniers of perception use it every day—their denial is not ignorance but self-interest.

Maturidi begins his refutation by exposing the deceptiveness of shaytan's whispers. He shows that those who reject sensory evidence in religious matters still act on it for worldly benefits, contradicting their own position. This lesson explores the first part of his argument, which establishes the real motive behind their denial.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage carefully
Read the Arabic passage and its translation to understand Maturidi's description of the denier's doubts and his response.
Pay attention to the opening statement about shaytan's role.
2
Identify the inconsistency
Notice how Maturidi points out that the denier of perception still avoids dangers and seeks pleasures based on perception. List specific examples from the text.
Examples: avoiding fires, eating food.
3
Understand the conclusion
Maturidi concludes that the denier's behavior proves his denial is not due to ignorance but love of pleasures. Reflect on how this refutes the skeptic's position.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ثم نذكر طرفا من الشبه التي اعترض من استجوذ [؟] عليه الشيطان وصرفه بها عما ظهر من البيان ليعلم أن الذي بعثه على ما اختار خدعة نفسه بتسويل عدوه، وذلك لا بتقصير من الله في نصب البرهان، ولا قوة إلا بالله. فنقول: سول الشيطان لمنكر العيان - بما قد يخرج على غير الذي حسبه المتأمل فيه ليناده [؟] عن عبادة الرحمن - المؤوف بصره، أو الذي تنازعه نفسه في المنام، أو الذي يبعد عنه، أو يدق عن الإحاطة، ثم لم يعمل عليه كيد الشيطان في الصرف عن الملاذ، وكف النفس عن الشهوات، ويوقيه من الجواهر المؤذية، وصون النفس عن اقتحام النيران والبحار، ولو كان عن حقيقة جهل ينطق لكان لا بقاء له، لما يقتحم المهالك، ويمتنع عن تناول الأغذية، فثبت أن الذي دعا إلى ما يقوله حب اللذات والميل إلى الشهوات. مع ما في الذي ذكر من اختلاف الأحوال. وتبين الخلاف دليل كاف على أنه قد علم العيان الخلاف ما ذكر من الحسبان. وعندنا أن ذلك بمعنى العيان: إن المؤوف، وفي حال المنام، والبعد، والدقة لا يصل إلى حقائق الأشياء وعند الارتفاع يصل. فذلك الذي أوجب من الإختلاف هو حق العيان، لم تجز أن ينكره، وعلى مثله قول مثبتي العيان، ومنكري الخبر بما قد يظهر فيه الكذب أن بعد أن ينتشر ب [؟] القول. ثم قد قيل: الإختبار في العيان اللذيذة والجواهر الشهية في الانتفاع، مما لولا الإخبار عما فيه من اللذة ما احتمل عاقل المخاطرة بنفسه من الإمتحان، وكذلك اتقاء المضار غير من سبق منهم الإمتحان، فما نالوا إلا بالإخبار وعلى ذلك المكاسب والحيل والحذر ونحو ذلك مما يرجع منافع ذلك إلى أبدانهم ودنياهم، وكذلك المضار. فثبت أن الذي بعث هذا إلى التكذيب ما في القول به من اثبات الحرمات، وكف النفس عن الشهوات، فيصير السبب الذي به خدع الشيطان هذا الصنف هو السبب الذي جامع الصنف الأول مع ما يوجد ذلك في العيان من الوجه الذي بينا، ولم يمنع هؤلاء القول به، فمثله في الأول؛ لأنه يظهر الكذب في الإخبار بما اعترض المخبر من الآفات التي تحملهم عليه.
Then we mention a part of the doubts that occurred to one upon whom shaytan gained mastery [؟] and diverted him by them from what appeared of the clarification, so that he would know that what drove him to what he chose is a deception of himself by the whispering of his enemy, and that is not due to a shortcoming from God in erecting the proof, and there is no power except through God. So we say: Shaytan instigated for the denier of perception ('iyan) - by what may come out contrary to what the contemplator supposed, to call him away [؟] from the worship of the Merciful - one whose sight is impaired, or one whose soul contends with him in sleep, or what is far from him, or what is subtle about encompassment, then he does not act according to the plot of shaytan in turning away from pleasures, and restraining the soul from desires, and protecting him from harmful substances, and guarding the soul from plunging into fires and seas. And if he were speaking from true ignorance, he would not survive, because he would plunge into dangers and refrain from consuming food. So it is established that what calls him to what he says is love of pleasures and inclination to desires. Along with what is mentioned of difference of states. And the clarification of the difference is sufficient evidence that he has known perception contrary to what was mentioned of estimation. And with us, that is by the meaning of perception: indeed, the one with impaired sight, and in the state of sleep, and distance, and subtlety cannot reach the realities of things, and when the obstacle is removed, he reaches. So that which necessitated the difference is the truth of perception; it is not permissible for him to deny it. And similar to it is the statement of the affirmers of perception and the deniers of report (khabar) by what may appear in it of falsehood after the statement spreads [؟]. Then it has been said: Testing in perception of pleasant things and desirable substances in benefit, were it not for the report about what is in them of pleasure, no rational person would risk himself in testing, and likewise avoiding harms without having previously tested them. So they only attained through report, and similarly earnings, tricks, caution, and the like, whose benefits return to their bodies and their worldly life, and likewise harms. So it is established that what drove this one to denial is what is in the statement of affirming obligations and restraining the soul from desires. So the cause by which shaytan deceived this group is the same cause that gathered the first group, along with what exists in perception from the aspect we explained, and these did not prevent the statement about it, so the same applies to the first; because falsehood appears in a report when the reporter is affected by afflictions that move him to it.
Source pages p. 624

Commentary
This passage is a refutation of those who deny perception ('iyan) and reports (khabar) as sources of knowledge, showing their inconsistency. Maturidi begins by stating that he will mention some doubts that shaytan instills to divert people from clear evidence, emphasizing that the fault lies in their own deception, not in God's proof. He describes specific types of doubters: those with impaired sight, those confused by dreams, those distant from an object, or those dealing with subtle matters. Yet these same people, when it comes to worldly pleasures and pains, act on perception and reports (e.g., they avoid harm and seek benefit). If they were truly ignorant, they would not survive. Hence, their denial of perception in religious matters is not due to genuine ignorance but to love of pleasures and desires. Maturidi then argues that differences in perception (e.g., impaired sight vs. normal sight, dream vs. wakefulness) do not negate the truth of perception itself; rather, they confirm it because when obstacles are removed, perception attains reality. He also compares deniers of reports: they accept reports in practical life (e.g., testing a delicious fruit based on someone's report) but reject them in religious matters. The conclusion is that the real cause of denial is the burden of religious obligations (hurmât) and self-restraint. The same cause that led the first group (deniers of attributes) also leads this group, and the inconsistency in their position reveals its falsity.

عيان
شبهة
جهل
لذات

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Deniers of perception are consistent skeptics who apply their method uniformly.
Correction: Maturidi shows they rely on perception for worldly benefits, so their denial in religious matters is motivated by desire for pleasure, not genuine skepticism.

Checkpoint

B) Because shaytan would kill him.
C) Because he would be unable to speak.
D) Because he would be isolated from society.

Key Takeaway
The denier of perception's own behavior reveals that his skepticism is not intellectual but driven by desire for pleasure.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?

?

?
If shaytan's deception works most effectively on your desires, which desire is currently keeping you from submitting to a proof that your heart already accepts?

Differences in Perception and the Defense of Reports
Maturidi defends perception against objections from variation, then defends reports using practical arguments.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand Maturidi's argument that differences in perception (e.g., impaired sight, dreams) do not negate its truth, and how he extends this reasoning to defend the validity of reports (khabar) against skeptics.

Core Idea
Differences in perception confirm its truth when obstacles are removed; reports are similarly indispensable and not invalidated by occasional falsehood.

Maturidi continues his refutation by addressing a common objection: perception varies due to impairments or distance. He argues that such variations actually prove the reality of perception when conditions are normal. He then draws a parallel to reports (khabar), showing that deniers of reports are similarly inconsistent. This lesson unpacks these arguments.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage carefully
Read the Arabic and translation, focusing on the examples of differences in perception (impaired sight, sleep, distance, subtlety) and the transition to reports.
2
Analyze the main argument about perception
Maturidi argues that when obstacles are removed (e.g., from sleep, distance), perception reaches its object. The fact that we can distinguish between correct and incorrect perception shows that perception is real. Identify this reasoning.
Note the phrase 'عند الارتفاع يصل' (when the obstacle is removed, he reaches).
3
Understand the extension to reports
Maturidi compares deniers of reports to deniers of perception. He gives the example of testing a fruit based on someone's report. Explain how this shows the necessity of reports in everyday life.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ثم نذكر طرفا من الشبه التي اعترض من استجوذ [؟] عليه الشيطان وصرفه بها عما ظهر من البيان ليعلم أن الذي بعثه على ما اختار خدعة نفسه بتسويل عدوه، وذلك لا بتقصير من الله في نصب البرهان، ولا قوة إلا بالله. فنقول: سول الشيطان لمنكر العيان - بما قد يخرج على غير الذي حسبه المتأمل فيه ليناده [؟] عن عبادة الرحمن - المؤوف بصره، أو الذي تنازعه نفسه في المنام، أو الذي يبعد عنه، أو يدق عن الإحاطة، ثم لم يعمل عليه كيد الشيطان في الصرف عن الملاذ، وكف النفس عن الشهوات، ويوقيه من الجواهر المؤذية، وصون النفس عن اقتحام النيران والبحار، ولو كان عن حقيقة جهل ينطق لكان لا بقاء له، لما يقتحم المهالك، ويمتنع عن تناول الأغذية، فثبت أن الذي دعا إلى ما يقوله حب اللذات والميل إلى الشهوات. مع ما في الذي ذكر من اختلاف الأحوال. وتبين الخلاف دليل كاف على أنه قد علم العيان الخلاف ما ذكر من الحسبان. وعندنا أن ذلك بمعنى العيان: إن المؤوف، وفي حال المنام، والبعد، والدقة لا يصل إلى حقائق الأشياء وعند الارتفاع يصل. فذلك الذي أوجب من الإختلاف هو حق العيان، لم تجز أن ينكره، وعلى مثله قول مثبتي العيان، ومنكري الخبر بما قد يظهر فيه الكذب أن بعد أن ينتشر ب [؟] القول. ثم قد قيل: الإختبار في العيان اللذيذة والجواهر الشهية في الانتفاع، مما لولا الإخبار عما فيه من اللذة ما احتمل عاقل المخاطرة بنفسه من الإمتحان، وكذلك اتقاء المضار غير من سبق منهم الإمتحان، فما نالوا إلا بالإخبار وعلى ذلك المكاسب والحيل والحذر ونحو ذلك مما يرجع منافع ذلك إلى أبدانهم ودنياهم، وكذلك المضار. فثبت أن الذي بعث هذا إلى التكذيب ما في القول به من اثبات الحرمات، وكف النفس عن الشهوات، فيصير السبب الذي به خدع الشيطان هذا الصنف هو السبب الذي جامع الصنف الأول مع ما يوجد ذلك في العيان من الوجه الذي بينا، ولم يمنع هؤلاء القول به، فمثله في الأول؛ لأنه يظهر الكذب في الإخبار بما اعترض المخبر من الآفات التي تحملهم عليه.
Then we mention a part of the doubts that occurred to one upon whom shaytan gained mastery [؟] and diverted him by them from what appeared of the clarification, so that he would know that what drove him to what he chose is a deception of himself by the whispering of his enemy, and that is not due to a shortcoming from God in erecting the proof, and there is no power except through God. So we say: Shaytan instigated for the denier of perception ('iyan) - by what may come out contrary to what the contemplator supposed, to call him away [؟] from the worship of the Merciful - one whose sight is impaired, or one whose soul contends with him in sleep, or what is far from him, or what is subtle about encompassment, then he does not act according to the plot of shaytan in turning away from pleasures, and restraining the soul from desires, and protecting him from harmful substances, and guarding the soul from plunging into fires and seas. And if he were speaking from true ignorance, he would not survive, because he would plunge into dangers and refrain from consuming food. So it is established that what calls him to what he says is love of pleasures and inclination to desires. Along with what is mentioned of difference of states. And the clarification of the difference is sufficient evidence that he has known perception contrary to what was mentioned of estimation. And with us, that is by the meaning of perception: indeed, the one with impaired sight, and in the state of sleep, and distance, and subtlety cannot reach the realities of things, and when the obstacle is removed, he reaches. So that which necessitated the difference is the truth of perception; it is not permissible for him to deny it. And similar to it is the statement of the affirmers of perception and the deniers of report (khabar) by what may appear in it of falsehood after the statement spreads [؟]. Then it has been said: Testing in perception of pleasant things and desirable substances in benefit, were it not for the report about what is in them of pleasure, no rational person would risk himself in testing, and likewise avoiding harms without having previously tested them. So they only attained through report, and similarly earnings, tricks, caution, and the like, whose benefits return to their bodies and their worldly life, and likewise harms. So it is established that what drove this one to denial is what is in the statement of affirming obligations and restraining the soul from desires. So the cause by which shaytan deceived this group is the same cause that gathered the first group, along with what exists in perception from the aspect we explained, and these did not prevent the statement about it, so the same applies to the first; because falsehood appears in a report when the reporter is affected by afflictions that move him to it.
Source pages p. 624

Commentary
This passage is a refutation of those who deny perception ('iyan) and reports (khabar) as sources of knowledge, showing their inconsistency. Maturidi begins by stating that he will mention some doubts that shaytan instills to divert people from clear evidence, emphasizing that the fault lies in their own deception, not in God's proof. He describes specific types of doubters: those with impaired sight, those confused by dreams, those distant from an object, or those dealing with subtle matters. Yet these same people, when it comes to worldly pleasures and pains, act on perception and reports (e.g., they avoid harm and seek benefit). If they were truly ignorant, they would not survive. Hence, their denial of perception in religious matters is not due to genuine ignorance but to love of pleasures and desires. Maturidi then argues that differences in perception (e.g., impaired sight vs. normal sight, dream vs. wakefulness) do not negate the truth of perception itself; rather, they confirm it because when obstacles are removed, perception attains reality. He also compares deniers of reports: they accept reports in practical life (e.g., testing a delicious fruit based on someone's report) but reject them in religious matters. The conclusion is that the real cause of denial is the burden of religious obligations (hurmât) and self-restraint. The same cause that led the first group (deniers of attributes) also leads this group, and the inconsistency in their position reveals its falsity.

Key Terms
عيان
خبر
اختلاف
حرمات
إختبار

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Variations in perception (e.g., optical illusions, dreams) prove that perception is unreliable and cannot be a source of knowledge.
Correction: Maturidi argues that such variations are due to obstacles and do not undermine the truth of perception when conditions are normal. They confirm that perception is real by showing when it fails and when it succeeds.

Checkpoint

B) Testing a fruit based on someone's report of its pleasure.

Key Takeaway
Differences in perception confirm its truth; reports are essential for worldly benefits, and their occasional falsehood does not warrant wholesale denial, which is instead driven by desire to avoid religious obligations.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?

?

?

The Argument from Needs Against Infinite Regress
Maturidi argues that needs necessitate a single cause, refuting infinite regress.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand Maturidi's argument that a chain of causes cannot go on infinitely, necessitating a first cause.

Core Idea
Needs point to a cause; an endless chain of needs is impossible.

Maturidi presents a concise argument against infinite regress. He begins with the observation that our needs and necessities indicate the existence of something else (a cause). He then argues that it is impossible for that cause itself to require another cause, and so on without end. This argument, though brief, is foundational in kalam for establishing the necessity of a First Cause.

Guided Path
1
Read the Arabic passage carefully
Read the Arabic passage once to grasp its flow. Notice the terms like 'ضروريات' and 'لا نهاية'. Then read the translation to confirm your understanding.
This passage is very concise; every word matters.
2
Understand the key terms
Identify 'ضروريات' (necessities) and 'حاجات' (needs). They are the starting point of the argument. Also note 'غير' (an other) and 'لا نهاية' (no end).
These terms are foundational for the logical structure.
3
Trace the logical flow
Follow the argument: Needs indicate an other (a cause). That cause cannot itself need another, because that would lead to a chain without end. Such an infinite regress is declared invalid (فاسد).
The conclusion is implicit: there must be a self-sufficient first cause.
4
Reflect on why infinite regress is invalid
Consider why an infinite chain of causes is considered invalid. In kalam, infinite regress is rejected because it would mean no ultimate explanation, which is rationally absurd.
This connects to the broader proof for God's existence.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وأصل آخر أيضا: أن الضروريات والحاجات هي التي دلت على غير. فلم يجز أن يحتمل ما احتمل هو لما يحوج إلى غير ثم ذلك إلى آخر إلى ما لا نهاية له، وذلك فاسد، والله أعلم.
And another principle also: that necessities and needs are what indicated an other. So it is not permissible that that which it itself [i.e., the need] indicates should need another, then that [needs] another, ad infinitum; that is invalid, and Allah knows best.
Source pages p. 628

Commentary
This passage presents an argument against infinite regress. The author states that necessities and needs point to something else (i.e., a cause). If that cause itself needs another cause, and so on without end, this chain is invalid (fāsid). The implication is that there must be a first cause that does not need another. This is a standard kalam argument for the existence of a Necessary Being.

Key Terms
ضروريات
حاجات
غير
لا نهاية
فاسد

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some people think an infinite chain of causes is possible and does not require a first cause.
Correction: Maturidi argues that an infinite regress of needs is invalid (فاسد) because it would mean no ultimate explanation, which is rationally absurd.

Checkpoint
What does the argument from needs and necessities conclude about an infinite chain of causes?
A) It is possible
B) It is invalid
C) It is necessary
D) It is unknowable

Key Takeaway
Maturidi's argument shows that an infinite chain of needs is impossible, requiring a self-sufficient first cause.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
1. You experience needs every day—hunger, thirst, dependence. Maturidi says these needs point to a cause beyond themselves. Have you ever paused to consider that your own constant neediness is a sign of a Self-Sufficient Creator? What would change in your daily life if you truly lived aware that every need you feel is a pointer to Allah, the Independent?
?
2. The argument says an infinite chain of needs is impossible. But what about the chains of needs in your own life—your reliance on people, circumstances, or possessions? Are you ever caught in a mental infinite regress of 'if only this happened, then I'd be satisfied'? How can you break that cycle by turning directly to the One who has no needs?
?
3. The passage concludes with 'that is invalid' (فاسد). Consider any belief or habit you hold that is based on a chain of assumptions that has no ultimate foundation. Are you living consistently with the truth that every good thing comes from a single, self-sufficient Source? Commit to one action today that reflects that reliance.

Eternal Chains Without a Creator
Maturidi presents two views on eternal causality.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand Maturidi's critique of the views that posit an eternal chain of causes without a creator.

Core Idea
Eternal causality without a Creator defies both reason and imagination.

Maturidi begins by presenting the first two opinions of those who claim the world is pre-eternal. One group argues for an endless chain of causes without a creator, while another admits a wise originator but still maintains an eternal cause-effect relationship. Both views, he argues, lead to logical absurdities.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage carefully
Read the Arabic passage and its translation to grasp the two views Maturidi presents.
Pay attention to the terms 'بلا منشئ' (without a creator) and 'بمنشي حكيم' (with a wise originator).
2
Identify the two views
Find where Maturidi describes the first group (endless chain without creator) and the second group (eternal cause with a wise originator).
3
Reflect on the critique
Consider Maturidi's objection: the first view negates reason by affirming the inconceivable; the second makes an eternal cause without effect problematic.
Maturidi uses the phrase 'آية نفي العقل' (sign of negation of intellect).

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قال أبو منصور: سنذكر أقاويل من يدعى قدم العالم، على ما عليه من كون شيء من شيء إلى ما لا نهاية له بلا منشئ، بما كذلك شهده دليل الغائب فيلزم ذلك في الذي غاب؛ لأنه لو جاز إيجاب خلاف الخيان بخلاف المعقول، على أن فيه إيجاب الخروج من التصور فى الوهم. والتقدر في العقل، وذلك آية نفي العقل، فمثله اعتقاد شيء لا من شيء نحو الأوقات، إنها تنفع تباعا، وقد اعتبرها بما لا وقت يتوهم إلا وأمكن توهم ذلك قبله إلى ما لا نهاية له، واعتبر أيضا بجواز البقاء بما لا يبقى. ومنهم من يقول يكون شيء بشيء إلى ما لا نهاية له بمنشي حكيم، وجعلوه علة كون العالم، ومحال كون العلة ولا معلول، مع ما لا يخلو من لا يوصف بالقدرة والجود فى القدم، وذلك آية العجز والحاجة، أو يوصف فيجب المقدور عليه وإفاضة الجود على كل شيء، وما ذكر من التوهم لهم أيضا. ومنهم من يقول بقدم الطينة وهي الأصل وحدث الصنعة. قال أبو منصور رحمه الله: فقوله بقدم الطينة لما ذكرنا من رفع كون شيء لا عن شيء، ثم كان كل شيء حدث عن شيء حدث عند انقلاب الأول وهلاكه نحو ما يحدث من النطفة والبيضة. ومنهم من جعل حدثه بعوارض حلت بالطينة فانقلبت على ما عليه الطبائع من الإعتدال والاختلاف. ومنهم من جعل حدثه بالباري. ومنهم من قال بالأصل وسماه هيولى. قال الشيخ أبو منصور رحمه الله: فجملة ما ذهب إليه هؤلاء دفع ما لا يتصور في الوهم، ولا يتمثل في النفس؛ إذ كذلك وجد، لم يحتمل قلوبهم إيجاب خلافه.
Abu Mansur said: We will mention the sayings of those who claim the pre-eternity of the world, based on their position that something comes from something endlessly without a creator, as such the evidence of the absent testified, so that follows in the case of what is absent; because if it were permissible to affirm contrary to what is contrary to the rational, this would involve affirming departure from conceptualization in the imagination and estimation in the intellect, and that is a sign of the negation of the intellect. Similarly is the belief in something from nothing, like times, they benefit successively, and he considered them by [the fact] that there is no time imagined except that it is possible to imagine something before it ad infinitum. He also considered [it] by the permissibility of remaining in what does not remain. Among them is one who says that something comes from something ad infinitum with a wise originator, and they made it the cause of the world's existence, and it is impossible for there to be a cause without an effect, along with [the fact] that he who is not described with power and generosity in pre-eternity is not free from [being] a sign of incapacity and need, or he is described [with them] and then what is predetermined and the outpouring of generosity on everything becomes necessary. And what is mentioned of imagination is also for them. Among them is one who says the pre-eternity of the clay, which is the origin, and the occurrence of the making. Abu Mansur (may Allah have mercy on him) said: His saying of the pre-eternity of the clay [is] due to what we mentioned of removing something from nothing, then everything that occurs came from something that occurred at the transformation and destruction of the first, like what occurs from the sperm and the egg. Among them is one who made its occurrence due to accidents that settled in the clay, and it transformed according to the natures of moderation and difference. Among them is one who made its occurrence by the Creator. Among them is one who said with the origin and called it hyle. The shaykh Abu Mansur (may Allah have mercy on him) said: The sum of what these people went to is the rejection of what is not conceivable in the imagination and not represented in the soul; for as such it was found, their hearts did not bear affirming its opposite.
Source pages p. 629

Commentary
This passage is a classification of the views of those who claim the pre-eternity of the world. Maturidi begins by stating his intention to mention the sayings of those who claim the world is pre-eternal. He then lists several positions. The first group holds that something comes from something in an endless chain without a creator, arguing from analogy with the observed world to the unseen. Maturidi notes that this involves affirming what is inconceivable in the imagination and intellect, which is a sign of the negation of reason. The second group posits a wise originator as the cause of the world's existence, but Maturidi points out the problem of an eternal cause without an effect. The third group asserts the pre-eternity of a prime matter (tin) and the occurrence of the artifact; Maturidi explains this as an attempt to avoid something coming from nothing. The fourth group attributes the world's occurrence to accidents that affect the prime matter. The fifth group attributes occurrence directly to the Creator. The sixth group posits an original principle called hyle. Maturidi concludes by summarizing that all these views ultimately reject what is inconceivable in the imagination and unrepresentable in the soul, as they could not accept affirming its opposite.

Key Terms
قدم العالم (qidam al-alam): pre-eternity of the world
علة (illah): cause

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What is the common problem Maturidi identifies with the first view (endless chain without a creator)?
A) It denies the existence of a Creator.
B) It relies on what is inconceivable in the imagination and intellect.
C) It assumes something comes from nothing.
D) It rejects the evidence of the senses.

Key Takeaway
Eternal causality without a creator or with an eternal cause-effect relation leads to rational absurdities.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Have you ever quietly assumed that the world could just go on forever without needing a Creator? How does the sheer absurdity of an endless chain of causes, as Maturidi describes it, challenge that assumption in your own heart? Will you let this sink in until it changes how you view the universe?
?
If you truly believe that God is all-powerful and all-generous, why do you sometimes live as if He is distant or inactive? The lesson shows that an eternal cause must have an effect—so what effect of God's power and generosity are you stifling in your life by your own negligence or doubt?
?
When you think about time before creation, does your mind feel uneasy? Maturidi says that trying to imagine an infinite past is a departure from reason. Do you trust your limited intellect enough to accept that some things are simply beyond it, or do you secretly think your own reasoning can grasp everything? What would humble acknowledgment of this look like in your daily prayer?

Prime Matter and Accidents
Maturidi presents views on eternal prime matter and its transformation.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the views that posit an eternal prime matter (clay or hyle) and the role of accidents in the world's occurrence.

Core Idea
Eternal prime matter avoids creation ex nihilo but still fails to explain change.

Maturidi continues by presenting several views that posit an eternal substratum—either clay (tinah) or hyle—from which the world is made. Some say the world occurs through accidents affecting this matter, while others attribute its occurrence directly to the Creator. These views attempt to avoid the problem of something coming from nothing.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage
Read the Arabic and translation for the views on prime matter and accidents.
Focus on the terms 'طينة' (clay) and 'هيولى' (hyle).
2
Identify the different positions
List the three distinct positions mentioned: (1) pre-eternity of clay with temporal making, (2) accidents on clay causing transformation, (3) occurrence directly by the Creator, (4) origin as hyle.
Note that Maturidi's own comment explains why some adopt the clay view.
3
Analyze Maturidi's response
Consider Maturidi's explanation that the clay view attempts to avoid something from nothing, but he critiques it as still relying on an eternal substrate.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قال أبو منصور: سنذكر أقاويل من يدعى قدم العالم، على ما عليه من كون شيء من شيء إلى ما لا نهاية له بلا منشئ، بما كذلك شهده دليل الغائب فيلزم ذلك في الذي غاب؛ لأنه لو جاز إيجاب خلاف الخيان بخلاف المعقول، على أن فيه إيجاب الخروج من التصور فى الوهم. والتقدر في العقل، وذلك آية نفي العقل، فمثله اعتقاد شيء لا من شيء نحو الأوقات، إنها تنفع تباعا، وقد اعتبرها بما لا وقت يتوهم إلا وأمكن توهم ذلك قبله إلى ما لا نهاية له، واعتبر أيضا بجواز البقاء بما لا يبقى. ومنهم من يقول يكون شيء بشيء إلى ما لا نهاية له بمنشي حكيم، وجعلوه علة كون العالم، ومحال كون العلة ولا معلول، مع ما لا يخلو من لا يوصف بالقدرة والجود فى القدم، وذلك آية العجز والحاجة، أو يوصف فيجب المقدور عليه وإفاضة الجود على كل شيء، وما ذكر من التوهم لهم أيضا. ومنهم من يقول بقدم الطينة وهي الأصل وحدث الصنعة. قال أبو منصور رحمه الله: فقوله بقدم الطينة لما ذكرنا من رفع كون شيء لا عن شيء، ثم كان كل شيء حدث عن شيء حدث عند انقلاب الأول وهلاكه نحو ما يحدث من النطفة والبيضة. ومنهم من جعل حدثه بعوارض حلت بالطينة فانقلبت على ما عليه الطبائع من الإعتدال والاختلاف. ومنهم من جعل حدثه بالباري. ومنهم من قال بالأصل وسماه هيولى. قال الشيخ أبو منصور رحمه الله: فجملة ما ذهب إليه هؤلاء دفع ما لا يتصور في الوهم، ولا يتمثل في النفس؛ إذ كذلك وجد، لم يحتمل قلوبهم إيجاب خلافه.
Abu Mansur said: We will mention the sayings of those who claim the pre-eternity of the world, based on their position that something comes from something endlessly without a creator, as such the evidence of the absent testified, so that follows in the case of what is absent; because if it were permissible to affirm contrary to what is contrary to the rational, this would involve affirming departure from conceptualization in the imagination and estimation in the intellect, and that is a sign of the negation of the intellect. Similarly is the belief in something from nothing, like times, they benefit successively, and he considered them by [the fact] that there is no time imagined except that it is possible to imagine something before it ad infinitum. He also considered [it] by the permissibility of remaining in what does not remain. Among them is one who says that something comes from something ad infinitum with a wise originator, and they made it the cause of the world's existence, and it is impossible for there to be a cause without an effect, along with [the fact] that he who is not described with power and generosity in pre-eternity is not free from [being] a sign of incapacity and need, or he is described [with them] and then what is predetermined and the outpouring of generosity on everything becomes necessary. And what is mentioned of imagination is also for them. Among them is one who says the pre-eternity of the clay, which is the origin, and the occurrence of the making. Abu Mansur (may Allah have mercy on him) said: His saying of the pre-eternity of the clay [is] due to what we mentioned of removing something from nothing, then everything that occurs came from something that occurred at the transformation and destruction of the first, like what occurs from the sperm and the egg. Among them is one who made its occurrence due to accidents that settled in the clay, and it transformed according to the natures of moderation and difference. Among them is one who made its occurrence by the Creator. Among them is one who said with the origin and called it hyle. The shaykh Abu Mansur (may Allah have mercy on him) said: The sum of what these people went to is the rejection of what is not conceivable in the imagination and not represented in the soul; for as such it was found, their hearts did not bear affirming its opposite.
Source pages p. 629

Commentary
This passage is a classification of the views of those who claim the pre-eternity of the world. Maturidi begins by stating his intention to mention the sayings of those who claim the world is pre-eternal. He then lists several positions. The first group holds that something comes from something in an endless chain without a creator, arguing from analogy with the observed world to the unseen. Maturidi notes that this involves affirming what is inconceivable in the imagination and intellect, which is a sign of the negation of reason. The second group posits a wise originator as the cause of the world's existence, but Maturidi points out the problem of an eternal cause without an effect. The third group asserts the pre-eternity of a prime matter (tin) and the occurrence of the artifact; Maturidi explains this as an attempt to avoid something coming from nothing. The fourth group attributes the world's occurrence to accidents that affect the prime matter. The fifth group attributes occurrence directly to the Creator. The sixth group posits an original principle called hyle. Maturidi concludes by summarizing that all these views ultimately reject what is inconceivable in the imagination and unrepresentable in the soul, as they could not accept affirming its opposite.

Key Terms
طينة (tinah): clay, prime matter
هيولى (hayula): hyle, prime matter

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to Maturidi, why do some people claim the pre-eternity of the clay?
A) To affirm the necessity of a Creator.
B) To avoid the idea of something coming from nothing.
C) To explain the diversity of natural forms.
D) To maintain the eternity of the world.

Key Takeaway
Positing an eternal prime matter avoids ex nihilo creation but fails to explain how change and temporality arise.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you consider the origin of the universe, do you ever subconsciously rely on 'eternal causes' like matter or nature to explain things, rather than fully resting in the fact that Allah created all from nothing? How does this lesson expose that tendency in your heart?
?
The philosophers proposed prime matter to avoid saying something comes from nothing. Is there an area in your spiritual life where you try to avoid admitting Allah's absolute power by holding onto familiar means and causes? Will you repent from that reliance and acknowledge that He alone is the origin of all things?
?
Maturidi critiques the view that change arises from accidents in matter. Have you ever attributed changes in your life to mere circumstances or 'natural processes' rather than seeing the hand of Allah in every transformation? What would it mean for you to truly see the Creator behind every change?

The Common Flaw: Rejecting the Inconceivable
Maturidi summarizes the common flaw of all views.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand Maturidi's overarching critique that all these views share the flaw of rejecting what is inconceivable in the imagination and unrepresentable in the soul.

Core Idea
All views on pre-eternity ultimately reject the rationally necessary.

Maturidi concludes his classification with a concise summary: the common thread among all these opinions is that they reject what cannot be conceived in the imagination or represented in the soul. Because they could not bear to affirm the opposite—that the world is created ex nihilo—they fell into speculative errors.

Guided Path
1
Read the final passage
Read Maturidi's concluding sentence, which encapsulates his critique of all the views.
This passage is short but dense.
2
Understand the key phrase
Focus on 'دفع ما لا يتصور في الوهم ولا يتمثل في النفس' (rejection of what is not conceivable in the imagination and not represented in the soul).
This is the core of Maturidi's argument.
3
Connect to previous lessons
Relate this conclusion to the specific views discussed in earlier lessons. How does each view illustrate this rejection?

Proof that Divine Action is by Choice
Al-Maturidi provides two rational arguments for divine choice.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the rational arguments that demonstrate Allah's actions are by choice, not by natural necessity.

Core Idea
Consistency and cycles in creation prove that God acts by choice, not nature.

Al-Maturidi presents two clear arguments from the observable world to establish a foundational point: that Allah's actions are free and chosen, not compelled by nature. As you read the passage, watch for how he uses the order of creation and the cycle of night and day to build his case.

Guided Path
1
Read the Arabic passage
Read the Arabic text once, then the translation. Notice the key terms: اتساق, اختيار, طبع.
2
Identify the first argument
Find the argument from consistency (اتساق الفعل المتوالى). How does order without corruption show choice?
3
Identify the second argument
Find the argument from creation-and-annihilation cycles (like night and day). Why can't a natural agent both create and destroy?
4
Understand the conclusion
Both arguments lead to the same conclusion: divine action is by choice. Reflect on why this matters for theology.
This refutes any notion of Allah acting by necessity.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وأيضا أن اتساق الفعل المتوالى بلا فساد يظهر، ولا خروج عن طريق يثبت كون المفعول بالاختيار من الفاعل، فثبت أن الخلق كان يفعله حقيقة، ولا قوة إلا بالله. وأيضا أن الله تعالى إذ أنشأ شيئا ثم أفناه، وفيه أيضا ما قد أعاده نحو الليل والنهار، ثبت أن فعله بالاختيار؛ إذ تحقق به صلاح ما قد أفسده، وإعادة ما قد أفناه، وإيجاد المعدوم وإعدام الموجود، فثبت أن طريق ذلك الاختيار؛ إذ من كان الذي منه يكون بالطبع لا يجيء منه نفي ما يوجد، وإيجاد ما يعدم، ولا قوة إلا بالله
And also that the consistency of successive action, without apparent corruption or deviation from the path, establishes that the effect is by choice from the agent. So it is established that the creation was truly His act, and there is no power except with Allah. And also that when Allah, may He be exalted, originated something then annihilated it, and in it also what He has restored, like night and day, it is established that His act is by choice; because by it is verified the rectification of what He had corrupted, and the restoration of what He had annihilated, and bringing into existence the non-existent and destroying the existent. So it is established that the way of that is choice; for whoever's action is by nature cannot bring about the negation of what exists nor the bringing into existence of what does not exist. And there is no power except with Allah.
Source pages p. 643

Commentary
This passage presents two rational arguments that Allah's actions are by choice (ikhtiyar) rather than by nature (tab'). The first argument: the consistent and orderly succession of events in creation, without corruption or deviation, indicates that the effect is by the agent's choice. The second argument: the cycle of creation, annihilation, and restoration (e.g., night and day) shows that the same agent can both create and destroy, which is impossible for a natural agent that acts only in one way. Therefore, divine action is by choice.

Key Terms
اختيار
طبع
فعل
إيجاد
إعدام
اتساق

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Thinking that God's actions are necessary like natural forces, denying His free will.
Correction: The passage shows that God's ability to create and destroy, and to maintain consistent order, requires that His actions be by choice, not by nature.

Checkpoint
What is the main conclusion from both arguments in this passage?
A) That creation is eternal.
B) That Allah's actions are by choice, not by nature.
C) That Allah's actions are caused by nature.
D) That Allah does not act at all.

Key Takeaway
Allah's actions are by choice, not by nature, as shown by the consistency of creation and the cycle of existence and annihilation.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you observe the consistent cycles of day and night, do you see them as mere natural laws, or do you see the deliberate choice of Allah behind them? How does this awareness change your sense of reliance on God today?
?
If Allah's actions were by nature, you would have no hope for forgiveness or change. But He acts by choice. What sin in your life are you taking for granted as inevitable? How does knowing that Allah can annihilate and restore transform your repentance?
?
The lesson shows that God brings into existence and destroys. Think of something you cling to as permanent. How does this truth reshape your attachment? What would it mean to entrust its existence to Allah's choice?

The Dilemma of Al-Ka'bi's Claim
Maturidi critiques Al-Ka'bi's view on divine choice via a dilemma.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand why stating that God’s actions are ‘by choice’ can lead to logical problems if not properly framed, as shown by Maturidi’s dilemma.

Core Idea
Saying God's actions are by choice implies a meaningless infinite regress.

Imam Maturidi begins by acknowledging Al-Ka'bi's statement but then shows its inconsistency with Al-Ka'bi's own principles. He presents a powerful dilemma that exposes the flaw in claiming God's actions are ‘by choice’ as a separate category.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage carefully
Read the Arabic passage once without analysing. Notice Al-Ka'bi's claim and Maturidi's initial comment.
The passage has some OCR uncertainty; focus on the logical structure.
2
Identify the two alternatives
Maturidi presents two possibilities: either creation is God's choice itself or it is other than His choice. Trace how each leads to a problem.
3
Understand the infinite regress argument
If creation is other than His choice, and it is an action, then it requires another choice, leading to an infinite chain—impossible because creation is finite.
This is the key logical move.
4
See the application to divine will
Maturidi notes that the same applies to those who affirm God's eternal will, which already is a choice for a thing at its time.
This links the critique to broader theological positions.
5
Reflect on the conclusion
Conclude why Maturidi says the statement is an error. The dilemma shows that the phrase ‘actions by choice’ is either redundant or contradictory.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وقال الكعبي: أفعال الله باختيار؛ لأن المطبوع يكون فعله نوعاً. قال أبو منصور رحمه الله: وما قاله حسن، وذلك مذهب أهل التوحيد لكنه لا معنى له على مذهبه؛ لما يقال الخلق اختياره أو غيره، وكذلك ما يقال في أفعاله. فإن قال: اختياره، فمعنى أفعاله إذا اختياره. فالقول بأن أفعال الله باختيار خطأ، بل هو اختيار ولا غير هنالك ليقال الذي قال: وإن قال: غير، فإما أن يكون فعله، فيجب أن يكون باختيار إلى ما لا نهاية له، وذلك محال؛ لأن الخلق متناه، أو هو فعل بلا اختيار، فيبطل قوله. وذلك يلزم من يصف الله بالإرادة في الأزل، وهي اختيار يكون شيء في وقته.

ثم الدلالة عندنا على الاختيار خروج الخلق على تفاوت [؟]، على ما من الحكمة، والدلالة على وحدانية الله، فدل ذلك على اختيار كون كل شيء على ما هو عليه، ولا قوة إلا بالله. ثم من يقول بخروج الخلق على ما عليه بالطبائع والأغذية، ومن يقول: ذلك عمل النجم والشمس والقمر، ومن يقول: ذلك بدوران الفلك، ومن يقول في التوالد بتدبير الآباء والأمهات، يرجع كله إلى كون شيء بشيء، إذا لم يثبت له أولية يبطل بالأدلة التي مر ذكرها، وإذا ثبت له أو لكل جنس من ذلك أولية، ثم استحال كونه بنفسه؛ لما يوجد نفسه إما حين خدمه، وذلك محال أن يوجد عديما، مع ما إذ رجع إليه تدبير كل شيء لا يحتمل أن يبلغه.
Al-Ka'bi said: God's actions are by choice (ikhtiyar), because the natural (matbu') has only one type of act. Abu Mansur (may Allah have mercy on him) said: What he said is good, and that is the school of the people of tawhid, but it has no meaning according to his school; because it is said that creation is His choice or other than that, and likewise what is said regarding His actions. If he says: it is His choice, then the meaning of His actions is [that they are] His choice. So the statement that God's actions are by choice is an error; rather, it is choice and there is no other [thing] there for one to say what he said. And if he says: other [than choice], then either it is His action, and then it must be by choice ad infinitum, which is impossible because creation is finite; or it is an action without choice, and thus his statement is invalidated. And that is entailed by describing God with will (irada) in pre-eternity, which is a choice of a thing coming to be at its time.

Then for us the evidence for choice is the emergence of creation with variation of its [essences?], in accordance with wisdom, and the evidence for God's oneness (tawhid). So that indicates choice for everything to be as it is. And there is no power except with Allah. Then those who say that creation emerges as it does by natures and nutriments, and those who say that is the work of the star, sun, and moon, and those who say that is by the rotation of the sphere, and those who say regarding generation by the design of fathers and mothers, all of it reduces to one thing coming from another thing. If an initial state is not established for it, it is invalidated by the proofs that have been mentioned. And if an initial state is established for it, or for each type of that, then it is impossible for it to exist by itself; because it would bring itself into existence either at the time of its service, that is impossible for a thing that does not exist to bring itself into existence, especially when the management of everything is referred back to it, it cannot reach it.
Source pages p. 659

Commentary
This passage is a refutation of Al-Ka'bi's claim that God's actions are by choice (ikhtiyar). Al-Ka'bi argued that the natural (matbu') has only one type of act (i.e., it acts uniformly), so God's actions being varied implies choice. Maturidi first praises the statement but then shows it is inconsistent with Al-Ka'bi's own school (presumably Mu'tazilism). He presents a dilemma: if one says creation is God's choice, then it is the choice itself, not an action done by choice—so saying 'actions by choice' is an error. If one says creation is other than His choice, then either it is His action (which would require another choice ad infinitum, impossible since creation is finite) or it is without choice (contradicting Al-Ka'bi). This dilemma also applies to those who affirm God's eternal will, which is a choice for a thing to occur at its time. Then Maturidi presents his own positive evidence (dilalah) for choice: the variation and wisdom in creation point to a single choice and to God's oneness. He then refutes alternative explanations (natures, astrology, celestial spheres, biological generation) by arguing that all such views reduce to one thing causing another, leading to an infinite regress unless an initial state is established, but then that initial state cannot bring itself into existence—this impossibility proves the need for a single divine choice.

Key Terms
اختيار
المطبوع
الفعل

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: That affirming God's actions are by choice is a straightforward, unproblematic statement.
Correction: Maturidi shows it leads to either redundancy or infinite regress, so it is not a simple affirmation.

Checkpoint
What is the central problem with Al-Ka'bi's statement that Maturidi identifies?
A) It implies that God's actions are natural and uniform.
B) It leads to an infinite regress if actions require choices ad infinitum.
C) It denies God's oneness.
D) It is not found in the Quran or Sunnah.

Key Takeaway
Maturidi demonstrates that claiming God's actions are by choice can lead to absurdity unless one understands that choice is not an attribute separate from action.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you say 'God acts by choice,' do you truly understand what you are affirming? Or are you repeating words without grasping their logical consequences? Will you examine your own beliefs with the same rigor Maturidi applies here, even if it unsettles you?
?
Maturidi shows that a seemingly innocent statement can lead to absurdity if not properly understood. Are there other beliefs you hold about Allah that you have never subjected to logical scrutiny? Will you commit to learning 'ilm al-kalam to ensure your faith is built on sound reasoning?
?
If a simple phrase like 'by choice' can be misapplied to God, how carefully must you weigh every word you speak about Him? Will you now take the time to study each attribute you affirm, so that your worship is based on truth and not on comfortable error?
