The Creation of Evil and the Response that It Is Mercy
Maturidi responds to the objection about evil and disease being mercy.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand Maturidi's argument that evils and diseases are not evil in wisdom but are mercy because they lead to repentance and deter from disobedience.

Core Idea
Evils and diseases are mercy in wisdom, not evil.

Maturidi addresses a common objection: if God creates evils and diseases, why not also create disbelief? The response is that such things are not evil in the divine plan; they are mercy, as they prompt repentance and deter sin. This lesson explores the structure of this argument and its deeper implications.

Guided Path
1
Read the objection and answer
Read the Arabic passage and its translation to understand the question and the initial response.
Note how the answer redefines the nature of evils.
2
Grasp the concept of 'mercy in wisdom'
Understand that evils are not evil from the perspective of divine wisdom; they serve a purpose.
The text says 'ليست بشرور في الحكمة'.
3
Explore Abu Mansur's elaboration
He explains how even the creation of disbelief can have wisdom, such as reminding of God's greatness.
This shows that all creation has a purpose.
4
Reflect on the act of the servant
The passage discusses the relationship between divine creation and human actions.
Consider how this relates to the broader topic of predestination.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وقد احتج بخلق القرآن بالتبعص والتجزئة ، فمثله فى كل الأعراض قائم، فيلزم القول به ، ولا قوة إلا بالله . ثم احتج لهم بخلق الشرور والأسقام ، وإن كانت ضارة ليم لا قلت في الكفر ؟ قال الفقيه : وهذا سؤال لا يسأله أحد على الابتداء إلا على المعارضة ، إذ لم يسم خالق هذه الأشياء بها وجب أن بخلقه أفعال الخلق بأسمائها ، يسمي وهذا نوع ما ليس لغيره فعل فى الحقيقة ، وفى أفعال الشرور ذلك . فأجاب هذه الأشياء ليست بشرور فى الحكمة ، بل هى رحمة بذكر التوبة وبزجر عن المعصية ، والكفر ليس بحكمة ألا بوجه ، تری أنه لا يجوز خلقه لا عن أحد ويجوز في الأول . قال أبو منصور رحمه الله : فالأول يقال له فى خلق فعل الكفر قبيحا ، وهو بذكر من عاينه عظيم فعله ، فيفزع إلى الله بالعصمة عنه بم يذكره / حدث الذي منه ، فيدعوه إلى التوحيد ، ثم يعرف به سفه من منه ذلك وفسقه ، و به يعرف اسمه وعواقبه ، ثم يعرفه أنه لا يضر الصانع ، ولا قوة إلا بالله وقوله : لا يخلقه لا أحد ، كلام من لا يعقل ما يقول وإلا فهو اسم لفعل العبد ، فكيف يكون ولا عبد ، وهذا لمن يقول التحرك هو زوال الجسم لا يخلقه دونه ، فيجب خلقه منه حكمة ، وعلى ذلك الأعراض وإمانة الخلق ، ولا قوة إلا بالله وهو جميع ثم الأسقام لا يجوز أن يخلقها لا في أحد ولا أحد ، ثم لم يمنع تحقق الحكمة لها ، فمثله الذي ذكر ، والله الموفق .
And he argued by the creation of the Quran through division and partitioning, so the like of that stands in every accident, so it is necessary to say it, and there is no power except with Allah. Then he argued for them by the creation of evils and diseases, and if they are harmful, why did you not say regarding disbelief? The faqih said: This is a question that no one asks in the first place except as an objection, since he did not name the creator of these things by them, so it is necessary that by His creation of the acts of the servants by their names, He names, and this is a type for which there is no act for other than Him in reality, and in the acts of evil is that. So he answered: These things are not evil in wisdom, but rather they are mercy through mentioning repentance and deterring from disobedience, and disbelief is not wisdom in any way. Do you see that it is not permissible to create it from no one, and it is permissible in the first? Abu Mansur (may Allah have mercy on him) said: The first is said to him about creating the act of disbelief as ugly, and it is by mentioning to him who witnesses the greatness of His act, so he flees to Allah for protection from it by what reminds him of the event from which it comes, so it invites him to tawhid, then he knows by it the foolishness of the one who does that and his wickedness, and by it he knows His name and its consequences, then he knows that it does not harm the Maker, and there is no power except with Allah. And his statement: He does not create it from anyone, is speech of one who does not understand what he says, otherwise it is a name for the act of the servant, so how can it be without a servant? And this is for those who say that movement is the removal of the body, He does not create it without him, so it is necessary to create it from him as wisdom, and upon that are all accidents and the trust of creation, and there is no power except with Allah. And then diseases are not permissible to create in no one, then the realization of wisdom for them is not prevented, so the like of what he mentioned, and Allah is the grantor of success.
Source pages p. 851

Commentary
This passage presents an objection about the creation of the Quran and then the creation of evils and diseases. The objection asks: if God creates evils, why not also create disbelief? The faqih responds that this question is only asked as an objection (muʿāraḍa), because the one who asks does not name the creator by these acts. He then answers that these things are not evil in wisdom (ḥikma); they are mercy (raḥma) because they lead to repentance and deter from disobedience. Disbelief itself is not wisdom. Abu Mansur elaborates: the creation of an act of disbelief can serve to remind one of God's greatness and lead to tawhid, thus it has a wise purpose. He also discusses the act of the servant: if movement is the removal of the body, then it must be created by the servant as an act. The passage concludes that diseases similarly have wisdom.

Key Terms
شرور
حكمة
رحمة
توبة
زجر
فعل العبد

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some may think the objection is about the justice of God creating evil, but it is actually about the consistency of attributing creation to God for both good and evil acts.
Correction: Maturidi shows that the objection is based on a misunderstanding: evils and diseases are not evil in wisdom but are mercy, so the analogy with disbelief fails.

Checkpoint
According to Maturidi, what is the true nature of evils and diseases?
A) They are purely evil and have no purpose
B) They are mercy in wisdom because they lead to repentance and deterrence
C) They are created by the servant, not by God
D) They have no wisdom at all

Key Takeaway
Evils and diseases are not evil in wisdom; they are mercy because they lead to repentance and deter from disobedience.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you face a trial or disease, do you see it as a mercy calling you to repent, or do you rebel against it? Will you commit today to viewing every hardship as a reminder from Allah?
?
How does this lesson challenge your view of your own sins? Can you accept that even your acts of disobedience, by their existence, can be a means for others to see Allah's greatness and turn to Him? What does that mean for your sense of shame?
?
The objector argued that if God creates evil, He should also create disbelief. The response says disbelief has no wisdom. Reflect: Is there any act of disobedience in your life that you consider 'wise' or justified? How does this lesson confront that justification?

Quranic Evidence That God Creates Human Actions
Maturidi cites Quranic verses and derives that God creates human acts.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how Maturidi uses Quranic verses to establish that God creates human actions, including faith and compassion.

Core Idea
God creates every human act, as Scripture shows.

Maturidi begins his argument by citing several Quranic verses where God directly attributes the creation of human qualities and actions to Himself. These verses serve as foundational evidence that human acts are not independent but are created by Allah. This lesson explores those verses and the conclusion Maturidi draws from them.

Guided Path
1
Read the Quranic citations
Read the verses Maturidi quotes: about placing compassion, inscribing faith, making houses from skins, and hardening hearts. Reflect on how each verse attributes the act to God.
2
Identify the common theme
Notice that all cited verses show God as the direct agent of these human attributes. This establishes a pattern.
3
Understand the conclusion
Maturidi concludes that since God condemns those who claim credit for what they did not do and obliges believers to thank Him for faith, faith is God's act. See how he builds from verses to theological principle.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
آياته وابتغاوكم من فضله ومن آياته ومن آياته، ومن البعيد إنشاء غيره له من الآيات؛ إذ ذلك الفاعل أحق أن تكون الآية له، وهن كلهن أفعال الخلق. وقال: "وَجَعَلْنَا فِي قُلُوبِ الَّذِينَ اتَّبَعُوهُ رَأْفَةٌ وَرَحْمَةٌ"، وقال: "أُولَئِكَ كَتَبَ فِي قُلُوبِهِم الإيمان"، وقال: "جَعَلَ لَكُم مِن جُلُودِ الأَنْعَامِ بُيُوتا"، وقال: "وَجَعَلْنا قُلُوبَهُم قَاسِيَةً"، وفي الجملة قال الله: "فَعَّالٌ لِمَا يُرِيدُ"، وفي أفعال العباد ما يريد، وقد وعد أن يفعل ما يريد، وقد ذم الله من أحب أن يحمد على ما لم يفعل، وقد ألزم المؤمنين أن يحمدوه على الإيمان، ثبت أن كان ذلك بفعله، ولا قوة إلا بالله. والأصل فيه أن دلالة خلق فعل كل أحد عنده أعظم من دلالة خلق السماوات والأرض فيما أريد تعرف حقيقة ذلك بالعقل أنه لا أحد امتحن قوى جواهر العالم حتى يعلم خروج كل شيء عن ذلك واحتمال خلق مثله، بل إنما يعرف ذلك بخروجه عن إمكان مثله، ومعلوم وجود أمور في غيره من الجواهر مما امتنع جوهره عن احتمال ذلك، نحو الطيران وإخراق الأشياء والسباحة بالجوهر وغير ذلك بقوى فيها، ويعلم كل أن ليس لأحد من الخلق تدبير في فعله، فيعلم بالضرورة بما خرج عن مقصوده وقصر عن الحد الذي يحده، وكان مقدرا بما لا يحتمل وسعه التقدير به، فيعلم به ضرورة أن الذي به قام هو الذي قدره وأخرجه على أراد، ولا قوة إلا بالله. مع ما لم يكن عند المعتزلة من الله إلى خلقه جملة سوى أنه أوجد بعد أن لم يكن، وأن الله لم يزل موجودا، وذلك المعنى في فعل كل أحد موجود، على أنه لولا الأمر والنهى لم يكن العقل يحتمل إخراج شيء عن قدرة الله وصرف شيء إلى فعل غيره، والأمر والنهى محل حق مع المعنى الذي يلزم القول به لولاهما لم يزل ذلك، فيكون المعروف بالعقل وما يوجبه ضرورة ذلك مدفوعا بالجهل بالحكمة بالحادث، ولو جاز ذلك لجاز إنكار الأمر والنهى بما كان في العقل من إثبات قدرة الله على كل شيء، بل قدرته على أشياء لا من شيء أو إحداث أعيان مثال أعجب من خلق فعل لآخر؛ إذ لولا ما للآخر من القدرة على ذلك لكان لا يضطرب، عاقل في تحقيق ذلك لله وقدرته، لا يجوز أن تنفى عن الله قدرة ذلك بعينه فيكون كالقادر على الشيء بغيره لا بنفسه، جل الله عن ذلك وتعالى لا عن قدرة العبد أو استطاعته.
His verses and that you seek of His bounty and from His verses and from His verses, and it is far off that another could produce verses for Him; for that agent is more deserving that the sign (ayah) belongs to him, and they [the signs] are all acts of the creatures. And He said: 'And We placed in the hearts of those who followed him compassion and mercy.' And He said: 'Those are the ones in whose hearts He has inscribed faith.' And He said: 'He made for you from the skins of cattle houses.' And He said: 'And We made their hearts hard.' And in summary, God said: 'Doer of whatever He wills.' And in the acts of the servants is what He wills, and He has promised to do what He wills, and God has condemned the one who loves to be praised for what he has not done, and He has obligated the believers to praise Him for faith. So it is established that that [faith] is by His act, and there is no power except with God. The principle in this is that the evidence of the creation of the act of everyone is greater in His sight than the evidence of the creation of the heavens and the earth in what is intended to be known. The reality of that by reason is that no one has examined the powers of the substances of the world so as to know the emergence of everything from that and the possibility of creating its like; rather, it is known only by its being beyond the possibility of its like. And it is known that there exist things in other substances which their substance is incapable of bearing, such as flying, piercing things, swimming with the substance, and other things by powers in them. And everyone knows that no creature has any management in his own act, so he knows by necessity, by what has come out of his intention and fallen short of the limit that he sets, and it was determined by what his capacity cannot bear to determine, so he knows by necessity that the one by whom it [the act] stands is the one who determined it and brought it forth according to what He willed. And there is no power except with God. Moreover, what is with the Mu'tazila from God to His creation in general is only that He brought into existence after non-existence, and that God has always existed, and that meaning exists in the act of everyone. And were it not for command and prohibition, reason would not tolerate excluding anything from God's power and attributing something to the act of another. And command and prohibition are the locus of truth with the meaning that one must affirm; without them that [meaning] would not cease. So what is known by reason and what its necessity requires is repelled by ignorance of wisdom in the temporal event. And if that were permissible, then denying command and prohibition would be permissible on the basis of what is in reason of affirming God's power over everything—rather His power over things from nothing or the creation of essences more wondrous than the creation of an act for another. For were it not that the other has power over that, an intelligent person would not be unsettled in affirming that to God and His power. It is not permissible to deny God's power of that very thing, lest He become like the one who is able over something by another, not by Himself. Exalted is God above that and high above the power of the servant or his capacity.
Source pages p. 854

Commentary
This passage presents a sustained argument by Maturidi that the creation of human actions provides stronger evidence for God's power than the creation of the heavens and earth. It begins by citing several Quranic verses where God attributes the creation of various things—like compassion in hearts, faith, houses, and hardness of hearts—to Himself, establishing that all such acts are His creation. Maturidi then argues that the evidence from the creation of every individual's act is greater, because reason cannot fully comprehend the creation of the cosmos, but every person experiences the limitation of their own power: they cannot produce an act at will, and their acts often fall short of their intentions. This proves that the act is determined and brought forth by God. The passage then addresses the Mu'tazila position, which holds that God only creates existence from non-existence and that human acts are independent. Maturidi argues that without the framework of command and prohibition, reason would not attribute any act to another agent. He further contends that denying God's power over human acts would lead to unacceptable consequences, such as making God's power dependent on another, which is blasphemy.

Key Terms
آية (sign)
فعل (act)
خلق (creation)
الإيمان (faith)

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some think human actions are independent of God's creation.
Correction: Maturidi shows through explicit Quranic verses that God creates even inner states like faith and compassion, so no act is independent.

Checkpoint
What conclusion does Maturidi draw from the verse 'Doer of whatever He wills'?
A) God only creates existence
B) In the acts of servants is what He wills
C) Humans are independent agents
D) Reason is superior

Key Takeaway
Through explicit Quranic verses, Maturidi establishes that God creates human actions, including faith and moral qualities.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Do you truly believe that your faith is a gift from God, not your own doing? How would your daily life change if you lived with that conviction every moment?
?
God condemns those who love to be praised for what they have not done. When you perform a good deed, do you feel a sense of ownership and pride? How can you train yourself to immediately attribute all good to Him?
?
The verse says God made hearts hard. Have you experienced a hardening of your own heart? In light of this lesson, what does that tell you about your need to constantly ask God to soften it?
